<p><b>Faisalabad</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small>pronunciation:</small> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <b>Lyallpur</b> until 1979), is the third-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_populated_metropolitan_areas_in_Pakistan" title="List of most populated metropolitan areas in Pakistan">most-populous city</a> in Pakistan, and the second-largest in the eastern province of <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a>. Historically one of the first planned cities within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>, it has long since developed into a cosmopolitan metropolis. Faisalabad was restructured into <a href="/wiki/City_district" title="City district">city district</a> status; a devolution promulgated by the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Pakistan" title="Local government in Pakistan">local government ordinance</a> (LGO). The total area of <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_District" title="Faisalabad District">Faisalabad District</a> is 58.56 km<sup>2</sup> (22.61 sq mi) while the area controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Development_Authority" title="Faisalabad Development Authority">Faisalabad Development Authority</a> (FDA) is 1,280 km<sup>2</sup> (490 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:8</sup> Faisalabad has grown to become a major industrial and distribution centre because of its central location in the region and connecting roads, rails, and air transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It has been referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> of Pakistan" because it contributes over 20% toward Pakistan's annual GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uaf.edu.pk_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-uaf.edu.pk-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2002_57_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2002_57-6">[6]</a></sup> Faisalabad's average annual GDP is $20.55 billion (USD),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd.27s_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd.27s-7">[7]</a></sup> of which 21% comes from agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:41</sup></p>
<p>The surrounding countryside, irrigated by the lower <a href="/wiki/Chenab_River" title="Chenab River">Chenab River</a>, produces cotton, wheat, sugarcane, vegetables and fruits. The city is an [industrial centre with major railway repair yards, engineering works, and mills that process sugar, flour, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_seed" title="Oil seed">oil seed</a>. Faisalabad is a major producer of superphosphates, cotton and silk textiles, hosiery, dyes, industrial chemicals, beverages, clothing, pulp and paper, printing, agricultural equipment, and <a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">ghee</a> (clarified butter). The Faisalabad Chamber of Commerce and Industry monitors industrial activity in the city and reports their findings to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_Pakistan_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Federation of Pakistan Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Federation of Pakistan Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a> and provincial government. The city has a major <a href="/wiki/Dry_port" title="Dry port">dry port</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_International_Airport" title="Faisalabad International Airport">international airport</a>.</p>
<p>Faisalabad is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Agriculture,_Faisalabad" title="University of Agriculture, Faisalabad">University of Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_College_University_(Faisalabad)" title="Government College University (Faisalabad)">Government College University</a> as well as the Ayub Agricultural Research Institute, <a href="/wiki/Divisional_Public_School_Faisalabad" title="Divisional Public School Faisalabad">Divisional Public School Faisalabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Textile_University" title="National Textile University">National Textile University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:13</sup> The city has its own cricket team, <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Wolves" title="Faisalabad Wolves">Faisalabad Wolves</a>, which is based at the <a href="/wiki/Iqbal_Stadium" title="Iqbal Stadium">Iqbal Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-8">[8]</a></sup> There are several other sports teams that compete internationally, including hockey and <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a> as well as other sporting events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PKT_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-PKT-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Agriculture,_Lyallpur,_British_India.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="500" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg/200px-University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg/300px-University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg/400px-University_of_Agriculture%2C_Lyallpur%2C_British_India.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The first university was built by the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> in 1906 with the foundation stone laying ceremony being laid by Sir Louis Dane, the then Lieut, and Governor of the Punjab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UAF:_History_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-UAF:_History-10">[10]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg"><img alt="" data-file-height="860" data-file-width="700" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg/200px-Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg/300px-Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg/400px-Quaid_E_Azam_Jinnah_Ali_Lyallpur_Dhobi_Ghat.jpeg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammed_Ali_Jinnah" title="Mohammed Ali Jinnah">Mohammed Ali Jinnah</a>, in Lyallpur where he gave an historic speech at Dhobi Ghat, circa 1943</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">

<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">One of the earlier industrial exhibition at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Agriculture" title="University of Agriculture">University of Agriculture</a> which is still a major exhibition held in the city today, circa 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span></h3>
<p>Faisalabad district actually began as Lyallpur district in 1904 and prior to that, was a <a href="/wiki/Tehsil" title="Tehsil">tehsil</a> of Jhang district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PGH_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-PGH-11">[11]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, the city Lyallpur was named in honour of the then Lieutenant-Governor of Punjab, Sir <a href="/wiki/James_Broadwood_Lyall" title="James Broadwood Lyall">James Broadwood Lyall</a>, for his services in the colonisation of the lower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chenab_Valley" title="Chenab Valley">Chenab Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asb.org.pk_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-asb.org.pk-12">[12]</a></sup> His surname Lyall was joined with "pur" which in old <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> language means city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanskrit_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sanskrit-13">[13]</a></sup> In the late 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Pakistan" title="Government of Pakistan">Government of Pakistan</a> changed the name of the city from Lyallpur to <i>Faisalabad</i> (meaning City of Faisal), in honour of <a href="/wiki/Faisal_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Faisal of Saudi Arabia">King Faisal of Saudi Arabia</a>, who made several financial contributions to Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCCI:City_History_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCCI:City_History-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_settlements">Early settlements</span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Faisalabad" title="University of Faisalabad">University of Faisalabad</a>, the city of Faisalabad traces its origins to the 18th century when the land was inhabited by a number of forest-dwelling tribes. It is believed these early settlements belonged to the ancient districts of <a href="/wiki/Jhang" title="Jhang">Jhang</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandalbar" title="Sandalbar">Sandalbar</a>, which included the area between <a href="/wiki/Shahdara" title="Shahdara">Shahdara</a> to Shorekot and <a href="/wiki/Sangla_Hill" title="Sangla Hill">Sangla Hill</a> to <a href="/wiki/Toba_Tek_Singh" title="Toba Tek Singh">Toba Tek Singh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TUF_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-TUF-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_rule">Colonial rule</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Punjab_1909.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="821" data-file-width="999" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Punjab_1909.jpg/200px-Punjab_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Punjab_1909.jpg/300px-Punjab_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Punjab_1909.jpg/400px-Punjab_1909.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Map of Punjab, circa 1909</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Partition_of_India-en.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="838" data-file-width="718" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Partition_of_India-en.svg/200px-Partition_of_India-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Partition_of_India-en.svg/300px-Partition_of_India-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Partition_of_India-en.svg/400px-Partition_of_India-en.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of India</a>, circa 1947</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the mid-18th century, the economic and administrative collapse of provinces within the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab" title="Punjab">Punjab</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a>, led to its dissolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-16">[16]</a></sup> Internal unrest resulted in multiple battles for independence and further deterioration of the region, which then led to formal colonialisation as established by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1858" title="Government of India Act 1858">Government of India Act 1858</a>, with direct control under the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a> from 1858 to 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stein_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stein-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duke_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duke-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1880, Poham Young <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Indian_Empire" title="Order of the Indian Empire">CIE</a>, a British colonial officer, proposed construction of a new strategic town within the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCF_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-DCF-19">[19]</a></sup> His proposal was supported by Sir James Broadwood Lyall and the city of Lyall was developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCF_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-DCF-19">[19]</a></sup> Historically, Faisalabad, (Lyallpur until 1979), became one of the first planned cities within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCUF_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCUF-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Young designed the city centre to replicate the design in the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a> with eight roads extending from a large <a href="/wiki/Clock_Tower,_Faisalabad" title="Clock Tower, Faisalabad">clock tower</a> at its epicentre;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCF-PP_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-DCF-PP-21">[21]</a></sup> a design geometrically symbolic of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">Cross of Saint Andrew</a> counterchanged with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_Patrick" title="Cross of Saint Patrick">Cross of Saint Patrick</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_George%27s_Cross" title="Saint George's Cross">Saint George's Cross</a> over all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The eight roads developed into eight separate bazaars (markets) leading to different regions of the Punjab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asb.org.pk_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-asb.org.pk-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UofF_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-UofF-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1892, the newly constructed town with its growing agricultural surplus was added to the British rail network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bogart_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bogart-24">[24]</a></sup> Construction of the rail link between <a href="/wiki/Wazirabad" title="Wazirabad">Wazirabad</a> and Lyallpur was completed in 1895.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCF-PP_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-DCF-PP-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1896, <a href="/wiki/Gujranwala" title="Gujranwala">Gujranwala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jhang" title="Jhang">Jhang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sahiwal" title="Sahiwal">Sahiwal</a> comprising the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tehsils" title="Tehsils">Tehsils</a> of Lyallpur were under the administrative control of the <a href="/wiki/Jhang_District" title="Jhang District">Jhang District</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PGH_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-PGH-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1904, the new district of Lyallpur was formed to include the tehsils of <a href="/wiki/Samundri" title="Samundri">Samundri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toba_Tek_Singh" title="Toba Tek Singh">Toba Tek Singh</a> with a sub-tehsil at <a href="/wiki/Jaranwala" title="Jaranwala">Jaranwala</a>, which later became a full tehsil in itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gazetteer_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gazetteer-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Agriculture_(Faisalabad)" title="University of Agriculture (Faisalabad)">University of Agriculture</a>, originally the Punjab Agricultural College and Research Institute, Lyallpur, was established in 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UAF:_History_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-UAF:_History-10">[10]</a></sup> The Town Committee was upgraded to a Municipal Committee in 1909. Lyallpur grew into an established agricultural tool and grain centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anwar_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anwar-26">[26]</a></sup> The 1930s brought industrial growth and market expansion to the textile industry as well as to food processing, grain crushing and chemicals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asb.org.pk_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-asb.org.pk-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp,_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="665" data-file-width="755" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg/200px-Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg/300px-Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg/400px-Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp%2C_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Mountbatten_among_the_Hindu_evacuees_at_the_Punjab_Scouts_Camp,_Layallpur_during_partition_of_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Edwina_Mountbatten,_Countess_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Edwina Mountbatten, Countess Mountbatten of Burma">Lady Mountbatten</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vicereine" title="Vicereine">Vicereine</a> of India, among the Hindu evacuees at the Punjab Scouts Camp, Layallpur during partition of India</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 1947, following three decades of nationalist struggles, India and Pakistan achieved independence. The British agreed to <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition colonial India</a> into two sovereign states – Pakistan with a <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> majority, and India with a <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> majority; however, more Muslims remained in India than what governing authorities believed would assimilate into Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup> The partitioning led to a mass migration of an estimated 10 million people which made it the largest mass migration in human history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup> India's <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> province was divided into <a href="/wiki/East_Pakistan" title="East Pakistan">East Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> (India), and the <a href="/wiki/Punjab_Province_(British_India)" title="Punjab Province (British India)">Punjab Province</a> was divided into <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab (West Pakistan)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab, India</a>. There were also respective divisions of the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Army" title="British Indian Army">British Indian Army</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Civil_Service" title="Indian Civil Service">Indian Civil Service</a>, various administrative services, the central treasury, and the railways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yale_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yale-28">[28]</a></sup> Riots and local fighting followed the expeditious withdrawal of the British, resulting in an estimated one million civilians deaths, particularly in the western region of Punjab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup> Lyallpur, which was located in the region of the Punjab Province that became West Pakistan, was populated by a number of <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a> who migrated to India, while <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> refugees from India settled in the district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yale_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yale-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1977, Pakistani authorities changed the name of the city to "Faisalabad" to honour the close relationship of <a href="/wiki/Faisal_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Faisal of Saudi Arabia">King Faisal of Saudi Arabia</a> with Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burki_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burki-29">[29]</a></sup> During the eighties, the city realised an increase in foreign investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune-26-April_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-26-April-30">[30]</a></sup> More Faisalabadis began working abroad as bilateral ties improved within the new dominion. This led to more monetary funds returning to the city that aided the development of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCCI:City_History_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FCCI:City_History-14">[14]</a></sup> In 1985, the city was upgraded as a division with the districts of Faisalabad, Jhang and Toba Tek Singh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TUF_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-TUF-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_public_services">Government and public services</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_Admin.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="368" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Faisalabad_Admin.PNG/200px-Faisalabad_Admin.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Faisalabad_Admin.PNG/300px-Faisalabad_Admin.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/78/Faisalabad_Admin.PNG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_Admin.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Faisalabad, a <a href="/wiki/City_Districts_of_Pakistan" title="City Districts of Pakistan">city district</a> with eight subdivisions:<br/>
1. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyallpur" title="Lyallpur">Lyallpur</a> Town<br/>
2. <a href="/wiki/Madina_Town" title="Madina Town">Madina Town</a><br/>

5. <a href="/wiki/Chak_Jhumra" title="Chak Jhumra">Chak Jhumra</a> Town<br/>
6. <a href="/wiki/Jaranwala" title="Jaranwala">Jaranwala</a> Town<br/>
7. <a href="/wiki/Samundri" title="Samundri">Samundri</a> Town<br/>
8. <a href="/wiki/Tandlianwala" title="Tandlianwala">Tandlianwala</a> Town</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_administration">Civic administration</span></h3>
<p>Faisalabad was restructured into <a href="/wiki/City_district" title="City district">city district</a> status; a devolution promulgated by the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Pakistan" title="Local government in Pakistan">local government ordinance</a> (LGO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRC_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRC-31">[31]</a></sup> It is governed by the <a href="/wiki/City_district" title="City district">city district</a>'s seven departments: Agriculture, Community Development, Education, Finance and Planning, Health, Municipal Services, and Works and Services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDG-32">[32]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_coordination_officer" title="District coordination officer">district coordination officer</a> of Faisalabad (DCO) is head of the city district government and responsible for co-ordinating and supervising the administrative units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDG-32">[32]</a></sup> Each of the seven departments has its own Executive District Officer who is charged with co-ordinating and overseeing the activities of their respective departments.</p>
<p>The aim of the city district government is to empower politics by improving governance which basically involved decentralising administrative authority with the establishment of different departments and respective department heads, all working under one platform. The stated vision and mission of the city district government of Faisalabad is to "establish an efficient, effective and accountable city district government, which is committed to respecting and upholding women, men and children's basic human rights, responsive towards people's needs, committed to poverty reduction and capable of meeting the challenges of the 21st century. Our actions will be driven by the concerns of local people."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDG-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tehsil_municipal_administration">Tehsil municipal administration</span></h3>
<p>In 2005, Faisalabad was reorganised as a city district composed of eight Tehsil municipal administrations (TMAs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faisalabad.gov:_Towns_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-faisalabad.gov:_Towns-33">[33]</a></sup> The functions of the TMA include preparation of the spatial and land use plans, management of these development plans and exercise of control over land use, land sub-division, land development and zoning by public and private sectors, enforcement of municipal laws, rules and by-laws, provision and management of water, drainage waste and sanitation along with allied municipal services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_TMA_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_TMA-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 118 <a href="/wiki/Union_councils_of_Pakistan" title="Union councils of Pakistan">union councils</a> in Faisalabad. Their role is to collect and maintain statistical information for socio-economic surveys. They consolidate ward neighbourhood development needs and prioritise these into union-wide development proposals. The council identifies any deficiencies in the delivery of these services and makes recommendations for improvement to the TMA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UCB_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-UCB-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faisalabad_Development_Authority">Faisalabad Development Authority</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Development_Authority" title="Faisalabad Development Authority">Faisalabad Development Authority</a> (FDA) was validly established in October 1976 under The Punjab Development of Cities Act (1976) to regulate, supervise and implement development activities in its jurisdiction area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The FDA acts as a policy-making body for the development of the city and is in charge of arranging and supervising major developments within the city. It is responsible for the administration of building regulations, management of parks and gardens and subsoil water management. The FDA works with the Water and Sanitation Agency (WASA) to control and maintain the water supply, sewerage and drainage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The FDA works to improve conditions in the slums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span></h3>
<p>Healthcare services are provided to the citizens by both public and private sector hospitals. The government–run hospitals are <a href="/wiki/Allied_Hospital" title="Allied Hospital">Allied Hospital</a>, District HQ Hospital, Institute of Child Care,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG:_FICC_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDG:_FICC-40">[40]</a></sup> PINUM Cancer Hospital, Faisalabad Institute of Cardiology (FIC) and General Hospitals in Ghulam Muhammadabad and Samanabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIC_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIC-41">[41]</a></sup> There are a number of private hospitals, clinics and laboratories in the city, notably Al-Rahmat labs, Mujahid Hospital lab, National Hospital lab &amp; Agha Khan lab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hosp_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hosp-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PPHCF_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-PPHCF-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span></h3>
<p>Law enforcement in Faisalabad is carried out by the city police, under the command of the city police officer (CPO), an appointment by the provincial government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawn-Feb_2007_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn-Feb_2007-44">[44]</a></sup> The office of the CPO is located in the District Courts, Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FPD_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FPD-45">[45]</a></sup> Various police formations include district police, elite police, traffic police, Punjab highway patrolling, investigation branch, and special branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Police_Formations_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Police_Formations-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>
<p>The Water and Sanitation Agency (WASA), is a subsidiary of Faisalabad Development Authority (FDA), established 23 April 1978 under the Development of Cities Act 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WASA:_Water_Supply_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-WASA:_Water_Supply-47">[47]</a></sup> 2015 estimates indicate that WASA provides about 72% of the city's sewerage services and about 60% of their water services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WASA:_Profile_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-WASA:_Profile-48">[48]</a></sup> The existing production capacity of WASA is 65 million imperial gallons per day (300 million litres per day), almost all of which is drawn from wells located in the old beds of the <a href="/wiki/Chenab_River" title="Chenab River">Chenab River</a>. From the wells, water is pumped to a terminal reservoir located on Sargodha Road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-49">[49]</a></sup> Water is normally supplied for a total of about 8 hours per day to the majority of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-49">[49]</a></sup> The Japan International Cooperation Agency (JICA) has provided financial and hardware equipment to help improve the water and sanitation conditions in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JICA:_WASA_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-JICA:_WASA-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span></h3>
<p>Faisalabad lies in the rolling flat plains of northeast <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a>, at 184 metres (604 ft) above sea level. The city proper comprises approximately 1,230 square kilometres (470 sq mi) while the district encompasses more than 16,000 square kilometres (6,200 sq mi). The Chenab River flows about 30 kilometres (19 mi), and the Ravi River meanders 40 kilometres (25 mi) to the southeast. The lower Chenab canal provides water to 80% of cultivated lands making it the main source of irrigation. Faisalabad is bound on the north by <a href="/wiki/Chiniot" title="Chiniot">Chiniot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheikhupura" title="Sheikhupura">Sheikhupura</a>, on the east by Sheikhupura and <a href="/wiki/Sahiwal" title="Sahiwal">Sahiwal</a>, on the south by Sahiwal and <a href="/wiki/Toba_Tek_Singh" title="Toba Tek Singh">Toba Tek Singh</a> and on the west by <a href="/wiki/Jhang" title="Jhang">Jhang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG:_Geography_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDG:_Geography-51">[51]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<p>The district of Faisalabad is part of the <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">alluvial plains</a> between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himalayan_foothills" title="Himalayan foothills">Himalayan foothills</a> and the central core of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-52">[52]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alluvial_deposits" title="Alluvial deposits">alluvial deposits</a> are typically over a thousand feet thick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasim_Akhtar_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nasim_Akhtar-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Interfluve" title="Interfluve">interfluves</a> are believed to have been formed during the <a href="/wiki/Late_Pleistocene" title="Late Pleistocene">Late Pleistocene</a> and feature <a href="/wiki/River_terraces_(tectonic%E2%80%93climatic_interaction)" title="River terraces (tectonic–climatic interaction)">river terraces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNAS_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-PNAS-54">[54]</a></sup> These were later identified as old and young floodplains of the <a href="/wiki/Ravi_River" title="Ravi River">Ravi River</a> on the Kamalia and Chenab Plains. The old floodplains consist of <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> deposits from the Ravi and Chenab rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jehangir_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jehangir-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The soil consists of young stratified silt loam or very fine sand loam which makes the subsoil weak in structure with common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kankers" title="Kankers">kankers</a> at only five feet. The course of the rivers within Faisalabad are winding and often subject to frequent alternations. In the rainy season, the currents are very strong. This leads to high floods in certain areas which do last for a number of days. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rakh" title="Rakh">Rakh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gogera" title="Gogera">Gogera</a> canals have encouraged the water levels in the district however the belt on the Ravi River has remained narrow. The river bed does include the river channels which have shifted the sand bars and low sandy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levees" title="Levees">levees</a> leading to river erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasim_Akhtar_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nasim_Akhtar-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faisalabad is situated at the centre of the lower <a href="/wiki/Rechna_Doab" title="Rechna Doab">Rechna Doab</a>, the area is located between the Chenab and Ravi rivers. There is a mild slope from the northeast to the southwest with an average fall of 0.2–0.3 metres per kilometre (1.1–1.6 feet per mile). The city is situated at an elevation of about 183 metres (600 ft). The topography is marked by valleys, local depression and high ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kobe_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kobe-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Faisalabad" title="Climate of Faisalabad">Climate of Faisalabad</a></div>
<p>The weather in the city is monitored by the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Meteorological_Department" title="Pakistan Meteorological Department">Pakistan Meteorological Department</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMD_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-PMD-57">[57]</a></sup> The Pakistan Meteorological Department regularly provides forecasts, public warnings and rainfall information to farmers with the assistance of the National Agromet Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMD-NAMC_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-PMD-NAMC-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMD-RAMC_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-PMD-RAMC-59">[59]</a></sup> Faisalabad has been classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (BWh) by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen-Geiger_climate_classification_system" title="Köppen-Geiger climate classification system">Köppen-Geiger climate classification system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate-Data_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-Data-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Average annual rainfall is approximately 375 millimetres (14.8 in) and highly seasonal. It is usually at its highest in July and August during monsoon season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kobe_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kobe-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_extreme_weather_records_in_Pakistan" title="List of extreme weather records in Pakistan">Record-breaking rainfall</a> of 264.2 millimetres (10.40 in) was recorded on 5 September 1961 by the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Meteorological_Department" title="Pakistan Meteorological Department">Pakistan Meteorological Department</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Observations from the Meteorological Observatory at the University of Agriculture indicate that overall rainfall levels in the city have increased by 90.4 millimetres (3.56 in) over the course of thirty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<table align="right" cellpadding="1" cellspacing="0" class="toccolours collapsible collapsed" style="margin:0 0 1em 1em; clear:right; text-align:right">

<p>Faisalabad was established as one of the first planned towns of British India covering an area of 3 square kilometres (1.2 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> It was initially designed to accommodate 20,000 people. The city's population increased from 69,930 in 1941 to 179,000 in 1951 (152.2% increase).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AUICK_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-AUICK-65">[65]</a></sup> Much of the increase is attributed to the settlement of Muslim refugees from East Punjab and <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a>, India. In 1961, the population rose to 425,248, an increase of 137.4%. Faisalabad set a record in the demographic history of Pakistan by registering an overall population increase of 508.1% between 1941 and 1961. The industrial revolution of the 1960s contributed to population growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AUICK_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-AUICK-65">[65]</a></sup> In 1961, the population was 425,248. A 1972 census ranked Faisalabad as the 3rd largest city of Pakistan with a population of 864,000. In a 1981 census, the population was 1,092,000; however, the Faisalabad Development Authority estimated the number to be 1,232,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AUICK_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-AUICK-65">[65]</a></sup> A 2014 demographic profile shows the population count at 3.038 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Omundi_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Omundi-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_and_ethnic_groups">Religion and ethnic groups</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg/200px-Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg/300px-Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg/400px-Sunni_Rizwi_Masjid.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A <a href="/wiki/Mughal_architecture" title="Mughal architecture">Mughal</a> inspired mosque in the old city. The majority of the population are Muslim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians-67">[67]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG/200px-Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG/300px-Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG/400px-Gurdwara-School_inner_front.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Gurudawar Layallpur, a <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> <a href="/wiki/Gurdwara" title="Gurdwara">Gurdwara</a> constructed during the reign of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> in 1911</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The province of Punjab, in which Faisalabad is the second largest city, has prevalent <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_system" title="Sociocultural system">sociocultural distinctions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAS_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAS-68">[68]</a></sup> Population sizes vary by district but some distinguishing factors include a young age structure, high age dependency ratio, a higher percentage of males, a higher proportion of married population, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heterogeneity" title="Heterogeneity">heterogeneity</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castes" title="Castes">castes</a> and languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAS_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAS-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:387</sup></p>
<p>Islam is the common heritage in the region with a 97.22% Muslim majority according to the 1998 Pakistan census report and 2001 population data sheet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAS_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-SAS-68">[68]</a></sup> Islamic influences are evident in the fundamental values of various inhabitants including cultural traditions, marriage, education, diet, ceremonies and policies with may reflect stark differences in rural villages as compared to urban areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJSER_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-IJSER-69">[69]</a></sup> People live in tight-knit joint families, although a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_family" title="Nuclear family">nuclear family</a> system is emerging due to changing socio-economic conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAS_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-SAS-68">[68]</a></sup> Ancient Pakistani culture prevails in most marriage practices in the region, as do certain restrictions related to ethnicity and caste. However, the influences of more modern societies have effected some change, particularly in the area of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dowry_system" title="Dowry system">dowry system</a>. As of 2016, monogamous and polygamous unions remain an acceptable marriage practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JASS_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-JASS-70">[70]</a></sup> In following ancient culture, marriages are customarily arranged by the parents or matchmakers. In some instances, the husband must buy his wife from her parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JASS_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-JASS-70">[70]</a></sup> Marriage ceremonies, which can be more or less formal, include rituals which are universal in nature and hold sociological importance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJSER_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-IJSER-69">[69]</a></sup> Studies conducted in 2007 and 2013, the latter in an outlying rural village in Faisalabad District, acknowledged the existence of gender bias and discrimination against females, stating that "Gender discrimination is not a new phenomenon", and that it still exists in the modern world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAS_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-SAS-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJSER_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-IJSER-69">[69]</a></sup> It was further noted that situations may be worse in villages because "whenever a girl is born, nobody celebrates her birth, whereas when a boy is born, it means great joy and celebration."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJSER_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-IJSER-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Social change in the region has been a slow process but there are indications that change has occurred as more villages are exposed to various forms of media and modernized urban communities. It is further noted that there has been a "conscious and persistent effort" to educate rural and urban societies about gender bias and equality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJSER_69-4"><a href="#cite_note-IJSER-69">[69]</a></sup> In early 2014, there was a march known as the "White Ribbon Campaign" which took place in front of the Faisalabad Press Club. Protestors appealed to the government to adopt new laws "to protect women who are discriminated against in the family and workplace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-AN-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prevalent minorities, particularly Hindu and Christian, feel a sense of vulnerability because of their religious beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians-67">[67]</a></sup> Labourers and farmhands comprise the countless Christian villages throughout Punjab; many are descendants of people who converted from Hinduism to Christianity under the British Raj, and considered low caste by virtue of their birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27">[27]</a></sup> A small population of wealthy, well-educated Christians have settled in Karachi; however, as a result of increasing Islamization, religious intolerance in Pakistani society, blashphemy laws and Islamist militancy, most have left Pakistan to settle in other countries where there is more religious tolerance, such as Canada and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_Pakistan.27s_Christians-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FNN_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FNN-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad,_the_City_of_Textile.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1070" data-file-width="1600" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg/200px-Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg/300px-Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg/400px-Faisalabad%2C_the_City_of_Textile.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metropk.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Metropk.jpg/200px-Metropk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Metropk.jpg/300px-Metropk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Metropk.jpg/400px-Metropk.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>

<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3064" data-file-width="5456" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG/200px-Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG/300px-Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG/400px-Ghanta_Ghar_04.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
