</div>
</div>
<p>Faisalabad contributes over 20% toward Pakistan's annual GDP; therefore, it is often referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> of Pakistan".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uaf.edu.pk_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-uaf.edu.pk-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2002_57_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2002_57-6">[6]</a></sup> Faisalabad's average annual GDP is $20.55 billion (USD),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd.27s_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd.27s-7">[7]</a></sup> of which 21% comes from agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:41</sup> The surrounding countryside, irrigated by the lower Chenab River, produces agricultural commodities such as cotton, rice, sugarcane, wheat, fruit and vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faisalabad_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Faisalabad-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune-12-2015_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-12-2015-74">[74]</a></sup> The city has carved a niche as an industrial centre with its highways, railways, railway repair yards, processing mills, and engineering works. It is a producer of industrial goods and textile manufacturing including cotton and silk textiles, super phosphates, hosiery, dyes, industrial chemicals, clothing, pulp and paper, printing, agricultural equipment, ghee (clarified butter), and beverages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DGTRDT_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-DGTRDT-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Faisalabad Chamber of Commerce and Industry monitors industrial activity in the city and reports their findings to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_Pakistan_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Federation of Pakistan Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Federation of Pakistan Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a> and provincial government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCCI:_History_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCCI:_History-76">[76]</a></sup> The city has a major <a href="/wiki/Dry_port" title="Dry port">dry port</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:25</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_International_Airport" title="Faisalabad International Airport">international airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPF_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-RPF-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:26</sup></p>
<p>Faisalabad is recognised as the centre of the textile industry in Pakistan, contributing to half of Pakistans total textile shipments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-77">[77]</a></sup> At the end of June 2012, textile mills employed 20% of the nation's workforce, and generated 1.3 trillion rupees ($13.8 billion) in textile products, most of which were exported to the US and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-77">[77]</a></sup> While Punjab's economy is driven primarily by agriculture, the textile industry along with leather products and light engineering goods play an important role, with more than 48,000 industrial units spread across Punjab.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMEDA_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMEDA-78">[78]</a></sup> In an effort to boost bilateral trade, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> have honorary-consulates in Faisalabad which enable trade links with the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Faisalabad clock tower and its eight bazaars (markets) remain a major trading zone in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Each of the eight bazaars has a special name and is known for selling certain goods as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Katchery Bazaar, named for the court (Katchery) is known for its mobile phone and accessory market.</li>
<li>Rail Bazar is a gold and cloth market.</li>
<li>Bhawana Bazaar supplies electrical and electronic goods.</li>
<li>Jhang Bazaar supplies fish, meat, vegetables and fruits.</li>
<li>Aminpur Bazaar supplies stationery and interior décor.</li>
<li>Kharkhana Bazaar is known for herbal medicines.</li>
<li>Gol Bazaar contains dry fruit, as well as wholesale soap, oil, and ghee shops.</li>
<li>Chiniot Bazaar is known for allopathic and homoeopathic medicinal stores, cloth, blankets, sofa cloth, and curtains. It also has poultry feed wholesale shops.</li>
<li>Montgomery Bazaar (also known as Sutar Mandi) is known for yarn and raw cloth trading.</li>
</ul>
<p>Faisalabad has received substantial funding from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Government of Punjab, Pakistan">government of Punjab</a> and the city district government to improve infrastructure and roads to rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Roads_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Roads-83">[83]</a></sup> In an effort to deal with the energy crisis, the FCCI has been working with private companies to develop renewable energy resources such as solar energy and the construction of dams within the district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR:_Dams_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR:_Dams-84">[84]</a></sup> CAE, a German-based renewable energy company, has disclosed plans to establish the first solar panel manufacturing facility in Faisalabad, second of its kind in Asia, with intentions of investing upwards of €100 million (Rs 12.9 billion) for its development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Solar_plant_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Solar_plant-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M2-2.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/M2-2.JPG/200px-M2-2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/M2-2.JPG/300px-M2-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/M2-2.JPG/400px-M2-2.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/M3_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M3 motorway (Pakistan)">M3</a> interchange connecting the <a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M2 motorway (Pakistan)">M2</a> and <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M4 motorway (Pakistan)">M4</a> is an important junction for the city where it connects the north and south of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_News:_Motorway_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_News:_Motorway-86">[86]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="1600" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg/200px-Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg/300px-Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg/400px-Faisalabad_D-Ground_Road.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Cars are driven on the <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">left hand side</a>, one of the remnants of the British empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_Alcock_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-James_Alcock-87">[87]</a></sup> The photograph above is a typical <a href="/wiki/Junction_(road)" title="Junction (road)">intersection</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Faisalabad is well-connected by rail, road and air. Public transportation in Faisalabad includes auto-rickshaws, buses and railways. <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_International_Airport" title="Faisalabad International Airport">Faisalabad International Airport</a> is located on the outskirts of the city, and operates flights to the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCAA_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCAA-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span></h3>
<p>The majority of roads are under the control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Highway_Authority_(Pakistan)" title="National Highway Authority (Pakistan)">National Highway Authority</a>, linking Faisalabad with other cities in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHA_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHA-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>National highways and motorways passing through Faisalabad</b></p>
<p>Faisalabad is connected to various parts of the country by several National Highways and Motorways:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHA_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHA-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:maps</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Trunk_Road" title="Grand Trunk Road">Grand Trunk Road</a>, otherwise known as GT Road, is the original highway that links Faisalabad to most parts of Pakistan as well as neighbouring countries. GT Road was the main highway that ran through the district before the completion of the motorways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPR-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/M3_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M3 motorway (Pakistan)">M3 motorway (Pakistan)</a> or M3 is an access-controlled motorway connecting Faisalabad with the <a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M2 motorway (Pakistan)">M2 motorway (Pakistan)</a> or M2 via the Pindi Bhattian Interchange. The M2 was the first motorway connecting Rawalpindi and Islamabad to Lahore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHA_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-NHA-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:6</sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M4 motorway (Pakistan)">M4 motorway (Pakistan)</a> or M4 is an access-controlled motorway connecting Faisalabad to <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a>. The M4 once complete will join the M5 which will run to the southern city of Karachi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M4_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-M4-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The district government has worked with the National Highway Authority to connect Multan and Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NESPAK_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-NESPAK-93">[93]</a></sup> The construction of the <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway_(Pakistan)" title="M4 motorway (Pakistan)">M4</a> is scheduled for completion by 2019. The new motorway will help reduce congestion, boost trade, and reduce travel times and transportation costs from Faisalabad, a major textile hub to the major trade centre of <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M4_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-M4-92">[92]</a></sup> One section of the M4 was inaugurated on 16 March 2015 which links Faisalabad to <a href="/wiki/Gojra" title="Gojra">Gojra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dunya:M4_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dunya:M4-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span></h3>
<p>The Faisalabad Urban Transport System Service (FUTS) is the main bus operator within the city. It was launched in 1994, and operates a number of large CNG buses and smaller <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hiace" title="Hiace">hiace</a> vans connecting the majority of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> There is another public-private run bus operator, Brothers Metro, which is a consortium between the government of Punjab and a private firm who operates a fleet of air-conditioned CNG buses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_CNG_Transport_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_CNG_Transport-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG/200px-Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG/300px-Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG/400px-Railway_station_of_Faisalabad.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The front entrance to the 19th century colonial railway station.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Railway_Platform.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Railway_Platform.jpg/200px-Railway_Platform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Railway_Platform.jpg/300px-Railway_Platform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Railway_Platform.jpg/400px-Railway_Platform.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">There are seven platforms at the station with a number of cargo sidings.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_railway_station" title="Faisalabad railway station">Faisalabad railway station</a> is the central railway station in the city. The railway line forms part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khanewal%E2%80%93Wazirabad_railway_line" title="Khanewal–Wazirabad railway line">Khanewal–Wazirabad railway line</a>. Rail services are operated by <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Railways" title="Pakistan Railways">Pakistan Railways</a>, owned and operated by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Railways_(Pakistan)" title="Ministry of Railways (Pakistan)">Ministry of Railways</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoR_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-MoR-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cargo Express services are operated by Pakistan Railways which runs from Karachi to Faisalabad via Multan. Twenty-seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogies" title="Bogies">bogies</a> comprise the goods train, and are handled respectively by private contractors at the station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawn:_Railway_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn:_Railway-98">[98]</a></sup> The station has a special cargo facility operated by the Ministry of Railways (Pakistan) for handling various goods from the city to other regions of the country. An express parcel service runs from Karachi to Lahore via Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Nation:_Parcel_Express_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Nation:_Parcel_Express-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_traffic">Air traffic</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="750" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg/200px-Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg/300px-Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg/400px-Faisalabad_Intl_Airport.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_International_Airport" title="Faisalabad International Airport">Faisalabad International Airport</a> is one of the top ten international airports in the country for air travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAA:_Traffic_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-CAA:_Traffic-100">[100]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_International_Airport" title="Faisalabad International Airport">Faisalabad International Airport</a> is approximately 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) from the city centre and is a major airport for domestic and international travel. The airport includes a cargo facility. As of January 2016, passenger flights are run by the national flag carrier, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines" title="Pakistan International Airlines">Pakistan International Airlines</a>, and a number of middle eastern carriers. There are seasonal Hajj operations to <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Shaheen_Air" title="Shaheen Air">Shaheen Air</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:Hajj_Flight_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:Hajj_Flight-101">[101]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FlyDubai" title="FlyDubai">FlyDubai</a> became the first international carrier to launch operations from the city followed by <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Arabia" title="Air Arabia">Air Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Air" title="Gulf Air">Gulf Air</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anna.aero_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-anna.aero-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gulf_Air_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gulf_Air-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, significant upgrades and renovations to the airport were initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Pakistan Civil Aviation Authority">Pakistan Civil Aviation Authority</a>, including updates to aviation technology, construction of additional areas and services for travellers, and the expansion of air traffic capabilities to accommodate wide-body aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_News:_Shujaat_Azeem_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_News:_Shujaat_Azeem-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Pakistan" title="Culture of Pakistan">Culture of Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Faisalabad" title="List of places in Faisalabad">List of places in Faisalabad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG/200px-Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG/300px-Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG/400px-Faisalabad_Arts_Council.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan Auditorium is home of the Faisalabad Arts Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune-March_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-March-105">[105]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2322" data-file-width="4128" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg/200px-Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg/300px-Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg/400px-Chicken_Fajita_Forkes_%26_Knives_Faisalabad.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Chicken jalfrezi pizza is made with spicy tandoori styled chicken, two types of cheese and mixed peppers.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club,_Faisalabad.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="793" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg/200px-Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg/300px-Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg/400px-Entrance_to_the_Chenab_Club%2C_Faisalabad.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Chenab Club is a social club built in 1904 and was inaugurated by British Officer Henry Cues. It was the first such club in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CC_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-CC-106">[106]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Faisalabad, the third most populated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_populated_metropolitan_areas_in_Pakistan" title="List of most populated metropolitan areas in Pakistan">metropolis</a> in Pakistan after <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-city-107">[107]</a></sup> is an epicentre for trade that has gained popularity for its colonial heritage sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In 1982, the Government of Punjab established the <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Arts_Council" title="Faisalabad Arts Council">Faisalabad Arts Council</a>, a division of the Punjab Arts Council which is overseen administratively by the Information, Culture and Youth Affairs Department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAC_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-109">[109]</a></sup> The Faisalabad Arts Council building, designed by architect Nayyer Ali Dada, was completed in 2006. The auditorium was named after the late <a href="/wiki/Nusrat_Fateh_Ali_Khan" title="Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan">Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan</a>, a Pakistani musician and singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAC_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span></h3>
<p>The Punjabi people celebrate a variety of cultural and religious festivals throughout the Punjab region, such as arts and craft, music, local events, and religious celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khalid_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Khalid-110">[110]</a></sup> The city of Faisalabad customarily celebrates its independence day on 14 August every year by raising the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistan_flag" title="Pakistan flag">Pakistan flag</a> at the clock tower in the Commissioner Office compound. Bazaars are colourfully decorated for the celebration, government and private buildings are brightly lit, and there are similar flag–raising ceremonies that are typically held in the district and its tehsils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ITN_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-ITN-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Independence_day_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Independence_day-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The arrival of spring brings the annual "Rang-e-Bahar" festival where the Parks &amp; Horticulture Authority of the city district government organise a flower show and exhibition at Jinnah Gardens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The University of Agriculture organises a similar event at their main campus which is known as the "Kissan Mela".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UAF:_Festivals_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-UAF:_Festivals-114">[114]</a></sup> The festival of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basant" title="Basant">Basant</a> which involves kite flying is an annual tradition in the city despite the ban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Basant_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Basant-115">[115]</a></sup> The provincial government introduced the "Canal Mela" which involves five days of festivities including the main canal in the city being decorated with national floats and lights ending with a musical concert to conclude the festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DT:_Canal_Mela_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-DT:_Canal_Mela-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Being a Muslim majority the city religious observances include <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mourning_of_Muharram" title="Mourning of Muharram">Muharram</a>. The festivals of <a href="/wiki/Chaand_Raat" title="Chaand Raat">Chaand Raat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a> are celebrated and are national holidays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Eid_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Eid-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">celebration</a> of the Prophet Muhammad birthday is observed in the city which is often referred to as "Eid Milād-un-Nabī".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Eid_Millad_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Eid_Millad-118">[118]</a></sup> There are a number of darbar and shrines which attract a number of devotees during the annual <a href="/wiki/Urs" title="Urs">Urs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_Shrines.2FTombs_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_Shrines.2FTombs-119">[119]</a></sup> There are a number of Christian churches in the city where Easter and Christmas services take place each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dunya:_Christmas_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dunya:_Christmas-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Christmas_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Christmas-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attire">Attire</span></h3>
<p>Traditional attire in Faisalabad is <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_clothing" title="Punjabi clothing">Punjabi clothing</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Dhoti" title="Dhoti">dhoti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurta" title="Kurta">kurta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pagri_(turban)" title="Pagri (turban)">pagri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-122">[122]</a></sup> Faisalabadi men wear white <a href="/wiki/Shalwar_kameez" title="Shalwar kameez">shalwar kameez</a> as do women but also with a <a href="/wiki/Dupatta" title="Dupatta">dupatta</a> (scarf). The more conservative women wear <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burqas" title="Burqas">burqas</a> that may or may not cover the face.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-122">[122]</a></sup> Combinations of Pakistani and Western attire are worn by women, such as an embroidered kurta worn with jeans or <a href="/wiki/Trousers" title="Trousers">trousers</a>, and half sleeve or sleeveless shirts with <a href="/wiki/Capri_pants" title="Capri pants">Capri pants</a>. Men have adopted some of the modern Western styles for both casual and formal business dress such as dress pants, trousers, T-shirts and jeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit_122-2"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faisalabad Institute of Textile and Fashion Design at the <a href="/wiki/Government_College_University_(Faisalabad)" title="Government College University (Faisalabad)">Government College University (Faisalabad)</a> teaches Fashion Design as part of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_Arts" title="Fine Arts">Fine Arts</a> program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCUF-Arts_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCUF-Arts-123">[123]</a></sup> Some of the more conservative establishments and universities follow strict dress codes, such as the National Textile University in Faisalabad where a notice was issued on 27 April 2016 by university professor Muhammad Ashfaq. The intent of the notice was to "promote a positive image of the NTU and to maintain good moral, religious and cultural values among the faculty, staff and students." The <a href="/wiki/Dress_code" title="Dress code">dress code</a> bans certain styles of Western attire including shorts, sleeveless shirts and shawls for men. Women are prohibited from wearing jeans, tights or <a href="/wiki/Leggings" title="Leggings">leggings</a>, sleeveless or half-sleeved shirts for women. Women are also prohibited from wearing heavy make-up and expensive jewellery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAMAA-TV_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAMAA-TV-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<p>Faisalabadi cuisine is very much <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_cuisine" title="Punjabi cuisine">Punjabi cuisine</a>, with influences from the realms of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_empires" title="Colonial empires">Colonial empires</a>. Key ingredients include rice or <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a> (flatbread) served with a vegetable or non-vegetable <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a>, a salad consisting of spiced tomatoes and onions, and yogurt. This is usually accompanied by a variety of <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_sweets" title="South Asian sweets">South Asian sweets</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jaggery" title="Jaggery">jaggery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gajar_ka_halwa" title="Gajar ka halwa">gajar ka halwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulab_jamun" title="Gulab jamun">gulab jamun</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jalebi" title="Jalebi">jalebi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jalebis_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jalebis-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tandoor" title="Tandoor">Tandoori</a> barbecue specialties consist of a variety of naan bread served with <a href="/wiki/Tandoori_chicken" title="Tandoori chicken">tandoori chicken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken_tikka" title="Chicken tikka">chicken tikka</a> or lamb <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shishkebab" title="Shishkebab">shishkebab</a> served with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mint_chutney" title="Mint chutney">mint chutney</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eat_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eat-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Street foods are a key element to Faislabadi cuisine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawn:_Food_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn:_Food-127">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samosa" title="Samosa">Samosas</a> (deep fried pastry filled with vegetables or meat) topped with an onion salad and two types of <a href="/wiki/Chutney" title="Chutney">chutney</a>. There is even a square dedicated to them in the old city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TP_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-TP-128">[128]</a></sup> Other street foods include, <a href="/wiki/Dahi_vada" title="Dahi vada">dahi bhale</a> (deep fried vadas in creamy yoghurt), <a href="/wiki/Panipuri" title="Panipuri">gol gappay</a> (fried round puri filled with vegetables and topped with tamarind chutney) and vegetable or chicken <a href="/wiki/Pakora" title="Pakora">pakoras</a>. <a href="/wiki/Biryani" title="Biryani">Biryani</a> and murgh pilao rice are a speciality in Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-QA-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>A typical breakfast in Faislabadi is <a href="/wiki/Halwa_poori" title="Halwa poori">halwa poori</a> comprising a deep fried flatbread served with a spicy chickpea curry and sweet orange coloured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halwa" title="Halwa">halwa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TP_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-TP-128">[128]</a></sup> It is customarily accompanied by a sweet or salty yoghurt based drink called <a href="/wiki/Lassi" title="Lassi">lassi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAMAA2_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAMAA2-130">[130]</a></sup> During winter, a common breakfast is <a href="/wiki/Naan" title="Naan">roghni naan bread</a> served with <a href="/wiki/Paya_(food)" title="Paya (food)">paya curry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pakladies_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pakladies-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Specialty drinks vary depending on climate. During winter, a variety of hot drinks are available, such as rabri doodh, a creamy dessert drink commonly made with full-fat milk, almonds, pistachios and basil seeds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doodh_Pati_Chai" title="Doodh Pati Chai">dhood patti</a> (milky tea), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kashmiri_chai" title="Kashmiri chai">Kashmiri chai</a>, a pink coloured milky tea containing almonds and pistachios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drink_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drink-132">[132]</a></sup> During summer, drinks such as sugar cane rusk, limo pani (iced lemon water), skanjvi (iced orange and black pepper) and <a href="/wiki/Lassi" title="Lassi">lassi</a> are common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aradmin_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aradmin-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are American-style fast food franchises that cater to the local community such as <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kentucky_Fried_Chicken_(KFC)" title="Kentucky Fried Chicken (KFC)">Kentucky Fried Chicken (KFC)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EJEFAS_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-EJEFAS-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literacy">Literacy</span></h3>
<p>According to a report by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Educational,_Scientific_and_Cultural_Organisation" title="United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organisation">United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organisation (UNESCO)</a>, the 2015 literacy rate for Pakistan ranked 160th which is among the lowest literacy rates in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Archivist_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Archivist-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981, Faisalabad was among four districts in Punjab, which included Gujranwala, Jhelum and Gujrat, that were experiencing low literacy rates, due primarily to either a lack of resources or family pressure; the latter of which may also be attributable to illiteracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Archivist_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Archivist-135">[135]</a></sup> In 1998, Faisalabad progressed to a higher literacy rate with the most improvement realised at the primary school level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-136">[136]</a></sup> In 2008, Faisalabad District ranked 51.9% which placed the district 9th in literacy out of the 34 Punjab districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aser_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aser-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, the city held its first literary festival which brought a number of writers to the city to encourage the community to follow the arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLF_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLF-138">[138]</a></sup> Two literary groups were established, the Faisalabad Union of Column Writers and Faisalabad Union of Journalists, to bring together printed media personalities for the purpose of providing training to budding writers from the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PPF_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-PPF-139">[139]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_open_spaces">Parks and open spaces</span></h3>
<p>Faisalabad is home to a number of parks, most of which are maintained by the Parks and Horticulture Authority, Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHA_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-PHA-140">[140]</a></sup> The oldest park in the city is Jinnah Garden, the city's central park, commonly known as "Company Bagh" and where the monument of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_James_Lyall" title="Sir Charles James Lyall">Sir Charles James Lyall</a> is situated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHA_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-PHA-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other parks include Canal Park, a family park located on the west bank of the Rakh Branch Canal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCCI:City_History_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-FCCI:City_History-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gatwala_Wildlife_Park" title="Gatwala Wildlife Park">Gatwala Wildlife Park</a> is a botanical natural reserve located at Gatwala that was renovated by the city district government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_Gatwala_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_Gatwala-141">[141]</a></sup> The Pahari Grounds near D Ground is another renovated park that has a Pakistan Air Force F-86 Sabre on display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Plantation_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Plantation-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sports_venues_in_Faisalabad" title="List of sports venues in Faisalabad">List of sports venues in Faisalabad</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is a popular sport in Faisalabad. Regional and international cricket matches are held in <a href="/wiki/Iqbal_Stadium" title="Iqbal Stadium">Iqbal Stadium</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-8">[8]</a></sup> named after Pakistani poet Sir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allama_Muhammad_Iqbal" title="Allama Muhammad Iqbal">Allama Muhammad Iqbal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NDTV:_Iqbal_Stadium_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV:_Iqbal_Stadium-143">[143]</a></sup> The stadium is home to Faisalabad's local team, the <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Wolves" title="Faisalabad Wolves">Faisalabad Wolves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNT_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-TNT-144">[144]</a></sup> Iqbal Stadium hosted the <a href="/wiki/1987_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1987 Cricket World Cup">1987 Cricket World Cup</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CA_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-CA-145">[145]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996 Cricket World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CA2_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-CA2-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad_Hockey_Stadium" title="Faisalabad Hockey Stadium">Faisalabad Hockey Stadium</a> located on Susan Road was constructed in 2002, and can accommodate 25,000 spectators. On 16 April 2003, the stadium was inaugurated by <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Maqbool" title="Khalid Maqbool">Khalid Maqbool</a>, governor of Punjab. It is the third largest <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> stadium in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawn_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn-147">[147]</a></sup> The stadium has hosted <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> matches for both national and international competition but by the beginning of 2016 was reported to be in "pathetic condition as its astroturf has completed its life span about eight years ago." Commissioner Naseem Nawaz advised that efforts were under way to maintain the stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawn_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2002, the Government College University established a Directorate of Sports to promote university and national level sports for male and female players. Infrastructure and facilities are available for university players in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_(sport)" title="Track (sport)">track</a>, hockey, tennis, basketball, table tennis, badminton and <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pitch" title="Cricket pitch">cricket pitch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCUF-Sports_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCUF-Sports-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_educational_institutions_in_Faisalabad" title="List of educational institutions in Faisalabad">List of educational institutions in Faisalabad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad,_Pakistan.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg/200px-Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg/300px-Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg/400px-Faisalabad%2C_Pakistan.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg/200px-Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg/300px-Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg/400px-Faisalabad_Pakistan_PSSP_06.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Department of Chemistry and Biochemistry is part of the Faculty of Sciences at the University of Agriculture (UAF).</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The population of Faisalabad has a literacy rate of approximately 60%, with a split of 69% for males and 46% for females (all figures are higher than the national average within the country).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Nation:_Literacy_rate_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Nation:_Literacy_rate-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faisalabad has several research and educational institutions, both public and private, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Agriculture,_Faisalabad" title="University of Agriculture, Faisalabad">University of Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_College_University_(Faisalabad)" title="Government College University (Faisalabad)">Government College University</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Textile_University" title="National Textile University">National Textile University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Institute_for_Agriculture_and_Biology" title="Nuclear Institute for Agriculture and Biology">Nuclear Institute for Agriculture and Biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Faisalabad" title="University of Faisalabad">University of Faisalabad</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Engineering_%26_Technology,_Lahore" title="University of Engineering &amp; Technology, Lahore">University of Engineering &amp; Technology of Lahore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HEC_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-HEC-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2014, the University of Agriculture ranked 1st in agriculture and 4th overall for universities in Pakistan according to the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Commission_of_Pakistan" title="Higher Education Commission of Pakistan">Higher Education Commission of Pakistan</a> (HEC), and was ranked 142nd in the 2013 Top 200 World Universities for agriculture and forestry by <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">Quacquarelli Symonds</a> (QS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune-December_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-December-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_system">Education system</span></h3>
<p>The education system is monitored by the District Education Officer of the City District Government of Faisalabad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDG:_Education_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDG:_Education-152">[152]</a></sup> The city government reports its findings to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Federal_Education_and_Professional_Training" title="Ministry of Federal Education and Professional Training">Ministry of Federal Education and Professional Training</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Education_(Pakistan)" title="Minister for Education (Pakistan)">Minister for Education</a>. Funding is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Government of Punjab, Pakistan">Government of Punjab, Pakistan</a>, City District Government and the fees collected from schools. There are four levels of the education system in the city: Primary, Elementary, High and Higher Secondary Level. Primary level education is only compulsory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KICC_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-KICC-153">[153]</a></sup> There are a number of schools for the assistance of children with <a href="/wiki/Special_needs" title="Special needs">special needs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_Special_Edu_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_Special_Edu-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries_and_museums">Public libraries and museums</span></h3>
<p>There are two <a href="/wiki/List_of_libraries_in_Pakistan" title="List of libraries in Pakistan">libraries</a> that are open to the public: Allama Iqbal Library and Municipal Corporation Public Library. They are funded and regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Government of Punjab, Pakistan">Government of Punjab, Pakistan</a> under the service sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_Libraries_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_Libraries-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Allama Iqbal Library is located on University Road, opposite the District Courts. The library is housed in the 1911-built colonial building originally named "Coronation Library" during the rule of the British Empire. In 2012, the building came under control of the Lyallpur Heritage Foundation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Museum_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Museum-156">[156]</a></sup> and the Punjab Archives and Libraries Department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET:_Libraries_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET:_Libraries-157">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyallpur_Museum" title="Lyallpur Museum">Lyallpur Museum</a> is located adjacent to the Allama Iqbal Library on University Road. It is a heritage museum and art gallery open to the public. The museum is primarily focused on regional history with a collection of artwork, artefacts and photographs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HB_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-HB-158">[158]</a></sup></li>
<li>Municipal Library is located in Iqbal Park on Narwala Road, opposite the historical grounds of Dhobi Ghat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ML_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-ML-159">[159]</a></sup> The library has a large collection of books, a photo gallery and a conference centre. In 2011, the library underwent a renovation costing 40 million rupees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PT-2011_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-PT-2011-160">[160]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Forest Library at the Punjab Forestry Research Institute (PFRI) is one of two specialist libraries, the other being in Lahore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_Forest_Library_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_Forest_Library-161">[161]</a></sup> Opened in 1986, the research library is based at the <a href="/wiki/Gatwala_Wildlife_Park" title="Gatwala Wildlife Park">Wildlife Research Center</a> in Gatwala.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-punjab.gov:_WRC_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-punjab.gov:_WRC-162">[162]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_radio">Television and radio</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Electronic_Media_Regulatory_Authority" title="Pakistan Electronic Media Regulatory Authority">Pakistan Electronic Media Regulatory Authority</a> (PEMRA) is responsible for the regulation and monitoring of electronic media entertainment in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEMRA_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-PEMRA-163">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Television_Corporation" title="Pakistan Television Corporation">Pakistan Television Corporation</a>, is the state-owned regulated television broadcasting network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMICC_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-AMICC-164">[164]</a></sup> The government began licensing private broadcasters in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internews_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Internews-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government of Pakistan installed the first radio transmitters in the city on 15 September 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBC:_Radio_Station_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBC:_Radio_Station-166">[166]</a></sup> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Pakistan" title="Radio Pakistan">Radio Pakistan</a>" broadcasts three government regulated FM stations: "Radio Pakistan FM101, Radio Pakistan FM93 and Radio Pakistan Sautul Qur'an Channel FM93.4. FM101 became operational in 2002, FM93 went live in 2010 and FM93.4 Sautul Qur'an Channel went live in 2016; PBC all three stations are standard power KW 2.5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBC:_FM_Station_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBC:_FM_Station-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Telecommunication_Authority" title="Pakistan Telecommunication Authority">Pakistan Telecommunication Authority</a> is a government-owned organisation that is responsible for the establishment, operation and maintenance of telecommunications in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PTA_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-PTA-168">[168]</a></sup> The organisation monitors and prevents illegal exchanges in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PTA2005_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-PTA2005-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PTCL" title="PTCL">Pakistan Telecommunication Company Limited</a> is the main provider of fixed line, mobile and broadband services. Regional headquarters is located at the Central Telecom House in Chinot Bazaar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PTCL_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-PTCL-170">[170]</a></sup> With the deregulation of the telecommunication sector by the Ministry of Information Technology, a range of companies now offer <a href="/wiki/List_of_mobile_network_operators_in_Pakistan" title="List of mobile network operators in Pakistan">mobile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Pakistan" title="Internet in Pakistan">broadband</a> services in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTO-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_theatre">Film and theatre</span></h3>
<p>In 2008, the Government of Pakistan lifted a forty-year ban on <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> films which allowed Indian films to be played in cinemas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AT_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-AT-172">[172]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Pakistan" title="Cinema of Pakistan">cinema industry</a> has since seen the introduction of new <a href="/wiki/List_of_cinemas_in_Pakistan" title="List of cinemas in Pakistan">cinemas</a> such as Cinepax by Hotel One,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinepax_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cinepax-173">[173]</a></sup> and Cine Nagina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCF_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCF-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Government College University in Faisalabad encourages students from the University of Agriculture to hold workshops and explore themes of peace and tolerance which can be used in an engaging and entertaining way to communicate complex issues to different audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CWSA_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-CWSA-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
